[?1049h[22;0;0t[?1h=
BASH(1)                               General Commands Manual                              BASH(1)[m
[m
[1mNAME[0m[m
       bash - GNU Bourne-Again SHell[m
[m
[1mSYNOPSIS[0m[m
       [1mbash[0m [options] [command_string | file][m
[m
[1mCOPYRIGHT[0m[m
       Bash is Copyright (C) 1989-2018 by the Free Software Foundation, Inc.[m
[m
[1mDESCRIPTION[0m[m
       [1mBash[0m  is an [1msh[0m-compatible command language interpreter that executes commands read from the[m
       standard input or from a file.  [1mBash[0m also incorporates useful features from the [4mKorn[24m and  [4mC[24m[m
       shells ([1mksh[0m and [1mcsh[0m).[m
[m
       [1mBash[0m  is  intended  to be a conformant implementation of the Shell and Utilities portion of[m
       the IEEE POSIX specification (IEEE Standard 1003.1).  [1mBash[0m can be configured to  be  POSIX-[m
       conformant by default.[m
[m
[1mOPTIONS[0m[m
       All  of the single-character shell options documented in the description of the [1mset[0m builtin[m
       command, including [1m-o[0m, can be used as options when the shell is invoked.  In addition, [1mbash[0m[m
       interprets the following options when it is invoked:[m
[m
       [1m-c[0m        If the [1m-c[0m option is present, then commands are read from the first non-option ar‚Äê[m
                 gument [4mcommand_string[24m.  If there are  arguments  after  the  [4mcommand_string[24m,  the[m
                 first  argument is assigned to [1m$0[0m and any remaining arguments are assigned to the[m
                 positional parameters.  The assignment to [1m$0[0m sets the name of the shell, which is[m
                 used in warning and error messages.[m
       [1m-i[0m        If the [1m-i[0m option is present, the shell is [4minteractive[24m.[m
       [1m-l[0m        Make [1mbash[0m act as if it had been invoked as a login shell (see [1mINVOCATION[0m below).[m
       [1m-r[0m        If  the  [1m-r[0m option is present, the shell becomes [4mrestricted[24m (see [1mRESTRICTED[0m [1mSHELL[0m[m
                 below).[m
       [1m-s[0m        If the [1m-s[0m option is present, or if no arguments remain after  option  processing,[m
                 then  commands  are  read  from the standard input.  This option allows the posi‚Äê[m
                 tional parameters to be set when invoking an interactive shell  or  when  reading[m
                 input through a pipe.[m
       [1m-v[0m        Print shell input lines as they are read.[m
       [1m-x[0m        Print commands and their arguments as they are executed.[m
       [1m-D[0m        A list of all double-quoted strings preceded by [1m$[0m is printed on the standard out‚Äê[m
                 put.  These are the strings that are subject to  language  translation  when  the[m
                 current  locale  is not [1mC[0m or [1mPOSIX[0m.  This implies the [1m-n[0m option; no commands will[m
                 be executed.[m
       [1m[-+]O[0m [1m[[0m[4mshopt_option[24m[1m][0m[m
                 [4mshopt_option[24m is one of the shell options accepted by the [1mshopt[0m builtin (see [1mSHELL[0m[m
                 [1mBUILTIN[0m  [1mCOMMANDS[0m  below).  If [4mshopt_option[24m is present, [1m-O[0m sets the value of that[m
                 option; [1m+O[0m unsets it.  If [4mshopt_option[24m is not supplied, the names and  values  of[m
                 the  shell  options accepted by [1mshopt[0m are printed on the standard output.  If the[m
                 invocation option is [1m+O[0m, the output is displayed in a format that may  be  reused[m
                 as input.[m
       [1m--[0m        A  [1m--[0m signals the end of options and disables further option processing.  Any ar‚Äê[m
                 guments after the [1m--[0m are treated as filenames and arguments.  An argument of [1m-[0m is[m
                 equivalent to [1m--[0m.[m
[m

[1mNAME[0m[m
       man - an interface to the on-line reference manuals[m
[m
[1mSYNOPSIS[0m[m
       [1mman[0m [[1m-C[0m [4mfile[24m] [[1m-d[0m] [[1m-D[0m] [[1m--warnings[0m[=[4mwarnings[24m]] [[1m-R[0m [4mencoding[24m] [[1m-L[0m [4mlocale[24m] [[1m-m[0m [4msystem[24m[,...]][m
       [[1m-M[0m [4mpath[24m] [[1m-S[0m [4mlist[24m] [[1m-e[0m [4mextension[24m] [[1m-i[0m|[1m-I[0m] [[1m--regex[0m|[1m--wildcard[0m]  [[1m--names-only[0m]  [[1m-a[0m]  [[1m-u[0m][m
       [[1m--no-subpages[0m] [[1m-P[0m [4mpager[24m] [[1m-r[0m [4mprompt[24m] [[1m-7[0m] [[1m-E[0m [4mencoding[24m] [[1m--no-hyphenation[0m] [[1m--no-justifi‚Äê[0m[m
       [1mcation[0m] [[1m-p[0m [4mstring[24m] [[1m-t[0m] [[1m-T[0m[[4mdevice[24m]] [[1m-H[0m[[4mbrowser[24m]] [[1m-X[0m[[4mdpi[24m]]  [[1m-Z[0m]  [[[4msection[24m]  [4mpage[24m[.[4msec‚Äê[24m[m
       [4mtion[24m] ...] ...[m
       [1mman[0m [1m-k[0m [[4mapropos[24m [4moptions[24m] [4mregexp[24m ...[m
       [1mman[0m [1m-K[0m [[1m-w[0m|[1m-W[0m] [[1m-S[0m [4mlist[24m] [[1m-i[0m|[1m-I[0m] [[1m--regex[0m] [[4msection[24m] [4mterm[24m ...[m
       [1mman[0m [1m-f[0m [[4mwhatis[24m [4moptions[24m] [4mpage[24m ...[m
       [1mman[0m [1m-l[0m [[1m-C[0m [4mfile[24m] [[1m-d[0m] [[1m-D[0m] [[1m--warnings[0m[=[4mwarnings[24m]] [[1m-R[0m [4mencoding[24m] [[1m-L[0m [4mlocale[24m] [[1m-P[0m [4mpager[24m] [[1m-r[0m[m
       [4mprompt[24m] [[1m-7[0m] [[1m-E[0m [4mencoding[24m] [[1m-p[0m [4mstring[24m] [[1m-t[0m] [[1m-T[0m[[4mdevice[24m]] [[1m-H[0m[[4mbrowser[24m]] [[1m-X[0m[[4mdpi[24m]] [[1m-Z[0m]  [4mfile[24m[m

       [1mman[0m [1m-c[0m [[1m-C[0m [4mfile[24m] [[1m-d[0m] [[1m-D[0m] [4mpage[24m ...[m
       [1mman[0m [[1m-?V[0m][m
[m
[1mDESCRIPTION[0m[m
       [1mman[0m  is the system's manual pager.  Each [4mpage[24m argument given to [1mman[0m is normally the name of[m
       a program, utility or function.  The [4mmanual[24m [4mpage[24m associated with each of these arguments is[m
       then  found  and  displayed.   A [4msection[24m, if provided, will direct [1mman[0m to look only in that[m
       [4msection[24m of the manual.  The default action is to search in all of  the  available  [4msections[24m[m
       following a pre-defined order ("1 n l 8 3 2 3posix 3pm 3perl 3am 5 4 9 6 7" by default, un‚Äê[m
       less overridden by the [1mSECTION[0m directive in [4m/etc/manpath.config[24m),  and  to  show  only  the[m
       first [4mpage[24m found, even if [4mpage[24m exists in several [4msections[24m.[m
[m
       The table below shows the [4msection[24m numbers of the manual followed by the types of pages they[m
       contain.[m
[m
       1   Executable programs or shell commands[m
       2   System calls (functions provided by the kernel)[m
       3   Library calls (functions within program libraries)[m
       4   Special files (usually found in [4m/dev[24m)[m
       5   File formats and conventions eg [4m/etc/passwd[24m[m
       6   Games[m
       7   Miscellaneous (including macro packages and conventions), e.g. [1mman[0m(7), [1mgroff[0m(7)[m
       8   System administration commands (usually only for root)[m
       9   Kernel routines [Non standard][m
[m
       A manual [4mpage[24m consists of several sections.[m
[m
       Conventional section names include [1mNAME[0m,  [1mSYNOPSIS[0m,  [1mCONFIGURATION[0m,  [1mDESCRIPTION[0m,  [1mOPTIONS[0m,[m
       [1mEXIT[0m [1mSTATUS[0m,  [1mRETURN[0m [1mVALUE[0m,  [1mERRORS[0m,  [1mENVIRONMENT[0m,  [1mFILES[0m,  [1mVERSIONS[0m, [1mCONFORMING[0m [1mTO[0m, [1mNOTES[0m,[m
       [1mBUGS[0m, [1mEXAMPLE[0m, [1mAUTHORS[0m, and [1mSEE[0m [1mALSO[0m.[m
[m
       The following conventions apply to the [1mSYNOPSIS[0m section and can be used as a guide in other[m
       sections.[m
[m
       [1mbold[0m [1mtext[0m          type exactly as shown.[m
       [4mitalic[24m [4mtext[24m        replace with appropriate argument.[m
       [[1m-abc[0m]             any or all arguments within [ ] are optional.[m
[7m Manual page man(1) line 1 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K

[K       [4margument[24m ...       [4margument[24m is repeatable.[m
[7m Manual page man(1) line 3 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K
[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB
[K       [[4mexpression[24m] ...   entire [4mexpression[24m within [ ] is repeatable.[m
[7m Manual page man(1) line 4 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K

APROPOS(1)                              Manual pager utils                              APROPOS(1)[m
[m
[1mNAME[0m[m
       apropos - search the manual page names and descriptions[m
[m
[1mSYNOPSIS[0m[m
       [1mapropos[0m  [[1m-dalv?V[0m]  [[1m-e[0m|[1m-w[0m|[1m-r[0m]  [[1m-s[0m [4mlist[24m] [[1m-m[0m [4msystem[24m[,...]] [[1m-M[0m [4mpath[24m] [[1m-L[0m [4mlocale[24m] [[1m-C[0m [4mfile[24m][m
       [4mkeyword[24m ...[m
[m
[1mDESCRIPTION[0m[m
       Each manual page has a short description available within it.   [1mapropos[0m  searches  the  de‚Äê[m
       scriptions for instances of [4mkeyword[24m.[m
[m
       [4mkeyword[24m  is  usually  a  regular  expression, as if ([1m-r[0m) was used, or may contain wildcards[m
       ([1m-w[0m), or match the exact keyword ([1m-e[0m).  Using these options, it may be necessary  to  quote[m
       the [4mkeyword[24m or escape (\) the special characters to stop the shell from interpreting them.[m
[m
       The  standard matching rules allow matches to be made against the page name and word bound‚Äê[m
       aries in the description.[m
[m
       The database searched by [1mapropos[0m is updated by the [1mmandb[0m program.  Depending  on  your  in‚Äê[m
       stallation,  this  may  be run by a periodic cron job, or may need to be run manually after[m
       new manual pages have been installed.[m
[m
[1mOPTIONS[0m[m
       [1m-d[0m, [1m--debug[0m[m
              Print debugging information.[m
[m
       [1m-v[0m, [1m--verbose[0m[m
              Print verbose warning messages.[m
[m
       [1m-r[0m, [1m--regex[0m[m
              Interpret each keyword as a regular expression.   This  is  the  default  behaviour.[m
              Each  keyword  will  be matched against the page names and the descriptions indepen‚Äê[m
              dently.  It can match any part of either.  The match is not limited to  word  bound‚Äê[m
              aries.[m
[m
       [1m-w[0m, [1m--wildcard[0m[m
              Interpret  each keyword as a pattern containing shell style wildcards.  Each keyword[m
              will be matched against the page names and the descriptions independently.  If [1m--ex‚Äê[0m[m
              [1mact[0m  is  also used, a match will only be found if an expanded keyword matches an en‚Äê[m
              tire description or page name.  Otherwise the keyword is also allowed  to  match  on[m
              word boundaries in the description.[m
[m
       [1m-e[0m, [1m--exact[0m[m
              Each keyword will be exactly matched against the page names and the descriptions.[m
[m
       [1m-a[0m, [1m--and[0m[m
              Only  display items that match all the supplied keywords.  The default is to display[m
              items that match any keyword.[m
[m
       [1m-l[0m, [1m--long[0m[m
              Do not trim output to the terminal width.  Normally, output will be truncated to the[m
              terminal width to avoid ugly results from poorly-written [1mNAME[0m sections.[m
[m
[7m Manual page apropos(1) line 1 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K
[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB
[K       [1m-s[0m [4mlist[24m, [1m--sections[0m [4mlist[24m, [1m--section[0m [4mlist[24m[m
[7m Manual page apropos(1) line 2 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K
[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB
[K              Search  only the given manual sections.  [4mlist[24m is a colon- or comma-separated list of[m
[7m Manual page apropos(1) line 3 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K

[K              sections.  If an entry in [4mlist[24m is a simple section, for example "3", then  the  dis‚Äê[m
[7m Manual page apropos(1) line 4 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K
[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB
[K              played  list  of descriptions will include pages in sections "3", "3perl", "3x", and[m
[7m Manual page apropos(1) line 5 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K
[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB
[K              so on; while if an entry in [4mlist[24m has an extension, for  example  "3perl",  then  the[m

CMAKE(1)                                       CMake                                      CMAKE(1)[m
[m
[1mNAME[0m[m
       cmake - CMake Command-Line Reference[m
[m
[1mSYNOPSIS[0m[m
          cmake [<options>] {<path-to-source> | <path-to-existing-build>}[m
          cmake [<options>] -S <path-to-source> -B <path-to-build>[m
          cmake [{-D <var>=<value>}...] -P <cmake-script-file>[m
          cmake --build <dir> [<options>...] [-- <build-tool-options>...][m
          cmake --open <dir>[m
          cmake -E <command> [<options>...][m
          cmake --find-package <options>...[m
[m
[1mDESCRIPTION[0m[m
       The  ‚Äúcmake‚Äù  executable  is the CMake command-line interface.  It may be used to configure[m
       projects in scripts.  Project configuration settings may be specified on the  command  line[m
       with the -D option.[m
[m
       CMake  is  a  cross-platform  build system generator.  Projects specify their build process[m
       with platform-independent CMake listfiles included in each directory of a source tree  with[m
       the  name  CMakeLists.txt.  Users build a project by using CMake to generate a build system[m
       for a native tool on their platform.[m
[m
[1mOPTIONS[0m[m
       [1m-S[0m [1m<path-to-source>[0m[m
              Path to root directory of the CMake project to build.[m
[m
       [1m-B[0m [1m<path-to-build>[0m[m
              Path to directory which CMake will use as the root of build directory.[m
[m
              If the directory doesn‚Äôt already exist CMake will make it.[m
[m
       [1m-C[0m [1m<initial-cache>[0m[m
              Pre-load a script to populate the cache.[m
[m
              When cmake is first run in an empty build tree, it creates a CMakeCache.txt file and[m
              populates it with customizable settings for the project.  This option may be used to[m
              specify a file from which to load cache entries before the first  pass  through  the[m
              project‚Äôs  cmake listfiles.  The loaded entries take priority over the project‚Äôs de‚Äê[m
              fault values.  The given file should be a CMake script containing SET commands  that[m
              use the CACHE option, not a cache-format file.[m
[m
       [1m-D[0m [1m<var>:<type>=<value>,[0m [1m-D[0m [1m<var>=<value>[0m[m
              Create or update a cmake cache entry.[m
[m
              When cmake is first run in an empty build tree, it creates a CMakeCache.txt file and[m
              populates it with customizable settings for the project.  This option may be used to[m
              specify  a setting that takes priority over the project‚Äôs default value.  The option[m
              may be repeated for as many cache entries as desired.[m
[m
              If the [1m:<type>[0m portion is given it must be one of the types specified by  the  [1mset()[0m[m
              command  documentation  for  its [1mCACHE[0m signature.  If the [1m:<type>[0m portion is omitted[m
              the entry will be created with no type if it does not exist with a type already.  If[m
              a  command in the project sets the type to [1mPATH[0m or [1mFILEPATH[0m then the [1m<value>[0m will be[m
[7m Manual page cmake(1) line 1 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K
